  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5143491f-04b7-4f37-b0e7-7aeeed153a99'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

      initializeSiwa();

At least, that’s what it feels like during her first week of junior year at her new ultra-intimidating prep school in Los Angeles.   <span id="freeText13738097384860155835" style="display:none">Everything about Jessie is wrong. At least, that’s what it feels like during her first week of junior year at her new ultra-intimidating prep school in Los Angeles. Just when she’s thinking about hightailing it back to Chicago, she gets an email from a person calling themselves Somebody/Nobody (SN for short), offering to help her navigate the wilds of Wood Valley High School. Is it an elaborate hoax? Or can she rely on SN for some much-needed help?<br /><br />It’s been barely two years since her mother’s death, and because her father eloped with a woman he met online, Jessie has been forced to move across the country to live with her stepmonster and her pretentious teenage son.<br /><br />In a leap of faith—or an act of complete desperation—Jessie begins to rely on SN, and SN quickly becomes her lifeline and closest ally. Jessie can’t help wanting to meet SN in person. But are some mysteries better left unsolved?</span>

        if (this.up('#box')) {

          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/1530663-lisa"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/1530663-lisa">Lisa</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I also found this really frustrating. It was so obvious from the first introduction of his character. I couldn't figure out if the author was trying t<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I also found this really frustrating. It was so obvious from the first introduction of his character. I couldn't figure out if the author was trying to keep readers guessing or just letting us watch her try to figure it out even though we know his real identity. I enjoyed the book overall but wish there'd been more mystery for the reader so that the payoff would have been more surprising and satisfying.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_1443613842" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1443613842" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30035966-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523817330p2/30035966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1443613842?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/30035966-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=5-star-favorites">5-star-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1443613842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10322109733165853640">I've never given a contemporary book 5 stars before (as far as I can remember... Is John green contemporary?!?! If so sorry I lied). <br/><br/><i>
  <b>"Perfect days are for people with small, realizable dreams. or maybe for all of us, they just happen in retrospect; they're only now perfect because they contain something irrevocably and irretrievably lost." </b>
</i><br/><br/>I'm finding this review hard to write... That typically happens when I'm so angry at a book that I can't even see straight. This isn't the problem I'm fac</span>
  <span id="freeText10322109733165853640" style="display:none">I've never given a contemporary book 5 stars before (as far as I can remember... Is John green contemporary?!?! If so sorry I lied). <br><br><i>
  <b>"Perfect days are for people with small, realizable dreams. or maybe for all of us, they just happen in retrospect; they're only now perfect because they contain something irrevocably and irretrievably lost." </b>
</i><br><br>I'm finding this review hard to write... That typically happens when I'm so angry at a book that I can't even see straight. This isn't the problem I'm facing with <i>TMTT. </i>I<i></i> liked it so much that there is so many things I want to say. I've truly never faced this issue before with a contemporary book before. It's my least favorite genre to read. Not including John Green books, I don't think I've ever been excited to finish a contemp book before this... I really thought about it too and nothing comes to mind. <br><br>I'm going to do this review a little different and stick with the common theme that <i>TMTT </i>and I'm going to tell you the three things that made me love this book. <br><br><b>1) The "Dear Reader" note. </b>I<b></b>t really isn't often I read these. This time I figured why the heck not. So glad I did. Julie explains why this book means so much to her, and why it was this book was so easy and so hard for her to write. She talks about the loss of her mother and how it really changed her whole life. This personally meant so much to me because I too lost my mother way before her time. What really hit home for me is when she quotes her main character Jessie. "<i>She will never see who I grow up to be-that great mystery of who I am and who I am meant to be-finally asked and answered"</i>. This hit way to close to home. It's such a selfish/non-selfish reason to think this, but it is so very true. It took me years to realize that my mother wouldn't be there for events and that's when everything really hits you. <br><br><b>2</b><b>) </b><b>Jessie. </b>She is an outstanding lead. She is the perfect combination of raw real human emotion and comical teenage girl. She gives the right emotions at the right time and talks to her age. She is beyond relatable and will completely pull you into her story. When Jess struggles, loves, gets lost you feel like you're right there with her. The funny dialog she manages to keep up through out this story is just great. Julie also hit the nail right on the head with how teenage girls think. Jessie's life has so many typical YA tropes in it that it could have easily taken this down a mundane path that would have ultimately lead to me having the same issues that I do with others. However Julie makes the typical something new and fresh. Jessie is a breath of fresh air along with all the other side characters. <br><br><b>3) The mystery. </b>When you read the synopsis of the book you figure out right away that there is basically a "who done it" style plot. Jessie starts receiving emails from an anonymous sender going by the username Somebody/Nobody (SN). This style would normally annoy the crap out of me. I've read plenty of books that have done this and almost 100% of the time I find myself skipping ahead, not caring about the story, getting bored, just not caring, and sneaking to find out the answer. With <i>TMTT </i>this wasn't at all the case. I was so interested in the story and going through things with Jessie that I didn't want to find out until the last possible second. The mystery as you can tell is all about who is SN. You, like Jessie, will go back and forth about who you think it will be. I will say that I had a pretty good idea about who it might have been, but I often found myself second guessing. Second guessing made reading this book so much fun. Warning: Julie will leave you guessing until the last second. The only thing I will suggest is that you keep maybe a little scrap piece of paper to write down the names of the guys in this book. Once all the key players were introduced once or twice I had to stop and remind myself who was who and who had what traits. When I jotted it down I was right back on track. Also kind of made me feel like I was playing a game of clue or something. <br><br><b><i>Tell Me Three Things </i>will without a doubt be my favorite contemporary all year. So thankful to have gotten an early copy of this, and am excited for others to get to read it too. This book has so much heart, so much fun to read, and left me with a huge giddy grin on my face. </b><br><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-fMStXLxaz58/Vls9afdAXEI/AAAAAAAACk0/9JCqwIg9hGQ/s1600/smile.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="178" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448820345ra/17194215.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br><b>READ THIS REVIEW AND OTHERS OVER ON OUR BLOG: <br><a href="http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">SBSR SBSR SBSR </a><br><a href="http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">SBSR SBSR SBSR </a><br><a href="http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">SBSR SBSR SBSR</a></b></span>

<div id="review_1614334553" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1614334553" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1614334553?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1614334553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9646132061713642940"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462418227i/18994694.jpg' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><strong>I was very excited to read this book</strong>. When I saw someone comparing it to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19547856.Simon_vs__the_Homo_Sapiens_Agenda' title='Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda by Becky Albertalli' rel='nofollow noopener'>Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda</a>, I immediately squeaked with delight!<br/><br/>I didn’t like it. At all. In fact, I don’t see why this newly released novel is so popular. I can think of dozens of novels dealing with similar themes that are funnier and a thousand times more gripping.<br/><br/>It started out just fine. There were e-mails exchanges and context for the story. Those were okay, really. That is, of course, before I got tired of the</span>
  <span id="freeText9646132061713642940" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462418227i/18994694.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong>I was very excited to read this book</strong>. When I saw someone comparing it to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19547856.Simon_vs__the_Homo_Sapiens_Agenda" title="Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda by Becky Albertalli" rel="nofollow noopener">Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda</a>, I immediately squeaked with delight!<br><br>I didn’t like it. At all. In fact, I don’t see why this newly released novel is so popular. I can think of dozens of novels dealing with similar themes that are funnier and a thousand times more gripping.<br><br>It started out just fine. There were e-mails exchanges and context for the story. Those were okay, really. That is, of course, before I got tired of the ubiquitous immatureness. Aren’t they supposed to be in high school? And 16-year-olds?<br><br><strong>This book is trying too hard. </strong><br><br>I read eighty pages before I realized that this was all déjà vu to me and that finishing this book would be pointless, if I was going to read what I’ve read countless times before. I wasn’t bored per se, but I felt like reading this book wouldn’t show me anything new.<br><br><strong>So I stopped.</strong> I wish I could say that I regret leaving the story, but the humour never even made me crack a nano-sized smile. That alone should justify my prematurely closing this book.<br><br>If you're looking for funny<em>, unputdownable</em>, original, epistolarish while incorporating the theme of death—though less intensely, I wholeheartedly recommend to you <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1189878.My_Most_Excellent_Year" title="My Most Excellent Year by Steve Kluger" rel="nofollow noopener">My Most Excellent Year</a>. If <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25893582.Tell_Me_Three_Things" title="Tell Me Three Things by Julie Buxbaum" rel="nofollow noopener">Tell Me Three Things</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1189878.My_Most_Excellent_Year" title="My Most Excellent Year by Steve Kluger" rel="nofollow noopener">My Most Excellent Year</a> were sparring with their words and humor, the last-mentioned would win for sure.<br><br><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/?a_aid=lolareviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">BD</a> | <a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="9646132061713642940" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2113695726" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5192154861319303507">let me tell you three things:<br/><br/><blockquote>1. this story is the ultimate meet cute of all meet cutes that have ever existed <br/>2. my cheeks received a world class workout from all the smiling reading this made me do<br/>3. this book was everything i could have hoped for and more</blockquote><br/>nothing puts me in a better mood than YA contemporary. nothing. its all the fluffy feels, the comedic romantic mishaps, the easily relatable characters, and the heartfelt messages that warm my cold heart. and this book was no exception. <br/><br/>it rea</span>
  <span id="freeText5192154861319303507" style="display:none">let me tell you three things:<br /><br /><blockquote>1. this story is the ultimate meet cute of all meet cutes that have ever existed <br />2. my cheeks received a world class workout from all the smiling reading this made me do<br />3. this book was everything i could have hoped for and more</blockquote><br />nothing puts me in a better mood than YA contemporary. nothing. its all the fluffy feels, the comedic romantic mishaps, the easily relatable characters, and the heartfelt messages that warm my cold heart. and this book was no exception. <br /><br />it really surprises me that julie buxbaum is such an underrated author - more people need to jump on her fan train because the woman can craft a story. it also probably helps that im a complete sucker for the whole ‘secret letters’ trope. but regardless, this book could cause type 2 diabetes, its that sweet. <br /><br />and i love that this story also talked about really deep and meaningful topics, but did so in a very approachable way. and it didnt lessen the adorableness of the book by any means. if anything, it only made it feel more genuine. i would recommend this to anyone looking for a great YA contemporary to easily fall in love with!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_1622568905" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1622568905" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1622568905?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1622568905" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15486205225134964619">I don't think I'll write a full review for this. It seems that all my GR friends loved it and I don't want to be that one party pooper who writes a negative review (again). <br/><br/>I'll just say that I made it about halfway before I couldn't take anymore of how almost every single girl but the special narrator is blonde, skinny, nearly naked, flirtatious and mean. Jessie is clearly supposed to be special and different from all of the “mostly blond, vacant-eyed Barbies and Kens.” <br/><br/>And the constant L.A. st</span>
  <span id="freeText15486205225134964619" style="display:none">I don't think I'll write a full review for this. It seems that all my GR friends loved it and I don't want to be that one party pooper who writes a negative review (again). <br /><br />I'll just say that I made it about halfway before I couldn't take anymore of how almost every single girl but the special narrator is blonde, skinny, nearly naked, flirtatious and mean. Jessie is clearly supposed to be special and different from all of the “mostly blond, vacant-eyed Barbies and Kens.” <br /><br />And the constant L.A. stereotypes were more annoying than funny. Maybe I don't have a right to be annoyed by this just because I've lived out here for a while, but some of them are just so blatantly untrue that it feels like the author knows nothing about the city. Everyone is definitely not skinny. Girls do not always wear skimpy dresses (in fact, L.A. is super casual compared to the U.K. and most people wear jeans and baggy tees). No, people do not always watch movies instead of reading. Girls are definitely not all blonde (high Hispanic and Asian population, actually). No, the grass is not always bright green just because it's always summer (sun + drought = not a good recipe for green grass).<br /><br />All of the humour relies heavily on melodrama and stereotypes, which is something that's never really appealed to me. I like more subtlety, and humour based on truth - because, if you ask me, there ain't anything funnier than reality. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25893582.Tell_Me_Three_Things" title="Tell Me Three Things by Julie Buxbaum" rel="nofollow noopener">Tell Me Three Things</a> was too heavy-handed to make me laugh.<br /><br />I kept trying to make excuses for it - that it was just supposed to be a lighthearted, funny book, but I couldn’t get past it. Guess it's a personal thing. I might just be wearing my grumpy pants today.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15486205225134964619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

</a><br/><br/><i>Tell Me Three Things</i> is a charming YA read that has the perfect amount of friendship, humor, emotion, and a touch of romance. <br/><br/>Lets start with Three things about this book: <br/><br/>1- There are three boys- and although they all have different good qualities, only one will be worthy of rooting for ;) <br/><br/> 2- There are some feels in this book, but it also made me laugh a good bit! <br/><br/>3- The end will leave you with a permagrin! <br/><br/><br/>Jessie is in her junior year of high school and is forced to move cross country fro</span>
  <span id="freeText8561510346177013504" style="display:none"><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/B3BAE4F6-537D-42C9-934E-CC2BA0AA5F45_zps13d6xuq5.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br><i>Tell Me Three Things</i> is a charming YA read that has the perfect amount of friendship, humor, emotion, and a touch of romance. <br><br>Lets start with Three things about this book: <br><br>1- There are three boys- and although they all have different good qualities, only one will be worthy of rooting for ;) <br><br> 2- There are some feels in this book, but it also made me laugh a good bit! <br><br>3- The end will leave you with a permagrin! <br><br><br>Jessie is in her junior year of high school and is forced to move cross country from Chicago to LA after her dad suddenly remarries. Her first day of school is rough. Then she gets an anonymous email. Somebody/Nobody AKA SN. This random and unknown person helps her through hard times, points her in the right direction when it comes to friends, and becomes a confidant of sorts. Even though Jessie has never met him (at least as far as she knows) they become close friends. <br><br>Eventually, life becomes a little easier for Jessie. She also starts to seriously wonder who SN is. There are three guys that she thinks could be it. The guy I liked best and had guessed was SN... well, it wasn’t much of a surprise for me. Regardless when I found out for sure I was grinning from ear to ear. I thoroughly enjoyed this YA read. I listened to the audiobook and the narration was good. I wish it wasn’t quite as predictable, but still a fantastic read! </span>

<div id="review_1626028652" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1626028652" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1626028652?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=from-publisher-author">from-publisher-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=unpopular-opinion">unpopular-opinion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=nope">nope</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1626028652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7083682384936213287">Uhhh.<br/><br/>So the situation is this: i'm out of contemporaries. Well, not completely, but I'm really close. The thing about that is that summer just started for me, and it's warm out and I have free time, and when the above information is true I WANT TO READ A LOT OF CONTEMPORARIES.<br/><br/>So I've been rereading. <br/><br/>I read this in summer 2016 and three-starred it. I remember it as being fun/fluffy/fine/cute/easy/etc. Good contemporary words.<br/><br/>Guess the hell what????<br/><br/>IT WASN'T.<br/><br/>What it was:<br/>- a three hundred page ode </span>
  <span id="freeText7083682384936213287" style="display:none">Uhhh.<br /><br />So the situation is this: i'm out of contemporaries. Well, not completely, but I'm really close. The thing about that is that summer just started for me, and it's warm out and I have free time, and when the above information is true I WANT TO READ A LOT OF CONTEMPORARIES.<br /><br />So I've been rereading. <br /><br />I read this in summer 2016 and three-starred it. I remember it as being fun/fluffy/fine/cute/easy/etc. Good contemporary words.<br /><br />Guess the hell what????<br /><br />IT WASN'T.<br /><br />What it was:<br />- a three hundred page ode to girl hate<br />- that's it, literally.<br /><br />Let's do some quotes, gang!<br /><br />---<br /><br /><b>LET'S TYPECAST AND EVISCERATE EVERY TEENAGE GIRL EVER</b><br /><br />It literally became a pain to transcribe all the examples of girl hate in this book. Like, I firmly believe that I spent roughly as much time one-handed typing these examples into my phone's notes app as I did actually reading and ingesting said vitriol.<br /><br />Friends, don't we love us some girl hate!!!<br /><br />A recurring theme in the girl hate of Tell Me Three Things - and it's one I've seen none too often let me tell you - is that teenage girls, in their entirety, like as a species, are unbelievably loud. None more so than in main character Jessie's new hometown in the Valley: <i>“the girls here are even louder, as if they think there’s a direct correlation between volume and male attention”</i>. Ah, yes, that combination of noisiness and male fixation we all associate with the female teen.<br /><br />And: <i>“There is something about her tone, quiet, like mine, that’s inviting. Not overly loud, not that teenage-girl voice that everyone else seems to use to demand notice.”</i> Now we're awarding merit based on low volume??? YOU'RE TELLING TEENAGE GIRLS TO BE QUIET????? Come the f*ck on.<br /><br />We're also granted the prize of some fun, descriptive phrases, like <i>"a revolting group of too-loud giggling girls"</i> (there's that loudness again!)<br /><br />Even the teachers get in on it: <i>“And I hate to say it, but girls in particular can be really cruel at your age.”</i> Really? Are you serious? Have you ever spoken to a teenage boy?? I don't wanna just flip gender roles here, but adolescent males have f*cked me over waaaaaayyyy more times than teenage girls have.<br /><br />Wait wait wait, before I forget - you know that thing of how all women want to have bulimia? No? Well this book sure does! <i>“According to Crystal, Gem’s out with a stomach flu and is ‘like, you know, puking her guts out, hashtag jealous.’”</i><br /><br />And just the slightest argument against women being in control of their own promiscuity: <i>“So my sister goes to UCLA, and she’s like this huge hobag there, right? And she says that sleeping with all these randos is her way of owning her sexuality.”</i> HA! Ridiculous! She thinks she can sleep with however many people she wants? She thinks it's her body? Hilarious!!<br /><br />Sometimes, it's just...weird: <i>“I quickly snap a selfie of me alone on a bench with my half-eaten peanut butter and jelly sandwich. I smile instead of pout, though, and label with the hashtag #Day14. Those blondes would pout, turn it into an</i> I’m so sexy <i>picture, and then Instagram it. </i>Look how hot I am not eating my sandwich!<i>"</i> Or, <i>“So it turns out Blond and Blonder did have an audience after all. Of course they did. Girls like that</i> always <i>have an audience.”</i> Uh, okay, Jessie. Take it down a notch. Especially with the blonde thing - we're sensitive, you know.<br /><br />But mostly, this girl hate comes with constant, incessant, unrelenting use of the word "bitch" (<i>“bitchy girls”</i> and <i>“She’s high with a vicarious bitch thrill”</i> were two I transcribed before I stopped writing them down, like, 20 pages in). But it's okay, because one time after Jessie uses the word - <i>“Have they always been so, you know, bitchy?”</i> - it's with a caveat. “I hate the word ‘bitch,’” Jessie promises. <i>“I do. Using the B-word makes me feel like a bad feminist, but sometimes there is no other word.”</i><br /><br />Oh, so even though you use the word bitch more times than I can count, you really hate it? You do? You promise? Oh, you call yourself a feminist in the midst of 300 pages of hating other women? Okay! All better!<br /><br />Plus, there's that typical “type of girl” line (along with its close relative, “one of those girls”). They say don't mess with the classics!!!<br /><br />Jessie pretty much explains all the toxicity goin' on within that little hate-filled head of hers: <i>“Whenever I meet someone new, I silently ask that inevitable catty girl question: is she prettier than me?”</i> If every girl is competition for your desperate insecurities, yeah, it makes sense that you'd develop a touch of a complex!<br /><br />---<br /><br /><b>YOU COASTAL ELITES</b><br /><br />A lot of the girl hate in this book is combined with another, less common but still thrilling type of hate: Californian hate/rich people hate/hippie hate??? I don't really know what to call it, but our main gal Jessie had to move from Chicago to California and she is <i>so mad about it</i>, you guys. Examples!<br /><br /><i>“So far, that’s the number one difference between LA and Chicago: all the girls here are thin and half-naked.”</i> Whaaaaat??? Half-naked???? (This came after a description of girls in sundresses with - gasp - dare I even say it? - spaghetti straps.)<br /><br /><i>“I thought the kids here only got excited about clothes and</i> Us Weekly <i>and expensive trips to pad their college applications.”</i> Hey, that one is just too far. Unsubstantiated. NO ONE likes <i>Us Weekly</i>.<br /><br /><i>“The women in LA all have taut skin, the kind pumped full of injectables that render them ageless, just as believably forty as seventy.”</i> This antifeminist manifesto just wouldn't be complete if we didn't touch on some plastic surgery-shaming.<br /><br />---<br /><br />I'm done with hate-filled quotes, so I'm just going to leave you with a cringe to end the night: <i>“You know what I heart? Nutella. And pajama pants. And an awesomesauce book.”</i><br /><br /><b>Bottom line</b>: I liked the ending of this book, and literally nothing else about it. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7083682384936213287" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1814564457" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1814564457" />
    <a title="Jennifer Kyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9916227-jennifer-kyle"><img alt="Jennifer Kyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514915429p2/9916227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1814564457?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Kyle" href="/user/show/9916227-jennifer-kyle">Jennifer Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/26242642-tell-me-three-things">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9916227-jennifer-kyle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1814564457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12566669861617231082"><b>5 STARS</b> <br/><br/><b>
  <i>”Tell me three things I don’t know about you.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479489349i/21197403._SY540_.jpg' width='430' height='470' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This a delightful, funny, solid, read that I highly recommend to friends who love a well done YA book. The story hit all the right buttons for me and left me with a huge smile on my face. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491912948ra/22460672.gif' width='430' height='150' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Two years following the death of her mother, Jessie’s father springs the fact that he has eloped on her. Jessie has to leave everything she knows in Chicago to move in with her new stepmother and her teenage son. Things aren't going so well for Jessie i</span>
  <span id="freeText12566669861617231082" style="display:none"><b>5 STARS</b> <br><br><b>
  <i>”Tell me three things I don’t know about you.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479489349i/21197403._SY540_.jpg" width="430" height="470" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This a delightful, funny, solid, read that I highly recommend to friends who love a well done YA book. The story hit all the right buttons for me and left me with a huge smile on my face. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491912948ra/22460672.gif" width="430" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Two years following the death of her mother, Jessie’s father springs the fact that he has eloped on her. Jessie has to leave everything she knows in Chicago to move in with her new stepmother and her teenage son. Things aren't going so well for Jessie it appears that her step brother seems completely disinterested in her. The kids in her new school seem to have known one another forever. While her father is just too happy to notice how hard this all is on her. It’s simply the new girl in school scenario done to perfection.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491912947ra/22460670.gif" width="430" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Jessie’s struggling to fit in at Wood Valley High School, she meets so many wonderful characters and with each male one she encounters she wonders if he could possibly be her SN. Who is SN? Well, out of the blue she receives helpful emails which later turn into text messages from “Somebody Nobody”. He seems to be perfect and definitely goes to her school. Yet she’s not sure which great guy he could be and is almost scared that he's not who she wants him to be.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479491792ra/21197997.gif" width="430" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>While Jessie acclimates to her new school and town she keeps contact with her best friend from home and slowly starts to make friends and find a job here in L.A. Her relationship with her stepbrother was well done as was her feelings and struggles to cope with the loss of her mom and this fancy home she now lives in. <br><br><b>
  <i>”Perfect days are for people with small realizable dreams. Or maybe for all of us, they just happen in retrospect; they’re only now perfect because they contain something irrevocably and irretrievably lost.”</i>
</b><br><br>Through the new friends she has made and her chats with the mysterious SN Jessie makes her own way in L.A. I adored how the author gifted Jessie the one thing everyone wants which is to feel truly seen and to feel known and that’s exactly what she has with SN. The reveal of SN had me on the edge of my seat. It is predictable yet I was terrified that he wasn't who I wanted him to be. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491912947ra/22460671.gif" width="430" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This is a very well done YA that goes on my favorites of the year list. All the characters were developed, the pacing perfect, and the ending is smile-inducing.<br><br><b>
  <i>”For real, It’s you?”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479489776ra/21197478.gif" width="430" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="12566669861617231082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1490261393" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1490261393" />
    <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata"><img alt="Faye, la Patata" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557835753p2/7650833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1490261393?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faye, la Patata" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata">Faye, la Patata</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=good-heroine">good-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=good-hero">good-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=best-books-i-ve-ever-read">best-books-i-ve-ever-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=kilig-to-the-bones">kilig-to-the-bones</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1490261393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2566349995555624116"><a href='http://wp.me/p3p0qg-1Li' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <b>PHILIPPINE RESIDENTS!!! FILIPINO BOOKWORMS! YOU CAN WIN A CHANCE TO READ THIS BOOK EARLY! JOIN MY GIVEAWAY HERE!</b>
</a><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453478535i/17833133._SY540_.png' alt='f5fcaa09a848bf8c79aaf4590520ca13' width='496' height='621' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The deepest smile on my face, the lightest feeling I've had for the longest while, a warmness surrounding my heart... these were the things I've felt while AND after reading this book. I went from <em>"Hmmm, this is interesting!"</em> to <em>"OMFG THIS IS THE CUTEST!!! MY HEART!!! ASDFGHJKL;"</em> in like a fraction of a second once the book reeled me in its grasp. And trust me, it didn't even try.<strong> </strong></span>
  <span id="freeText2566349995555624116" style="display:none"><a href="http://wp.me/p3p0qg-1Li" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>PHILIPPINE RESIDENTS!!! FILIPINO BOOKWORMS! YOU CAN WIN A CHANCE TO READ THIS BOOK EARLY! JOIN MY GIVEAWAY HERE!</b>
</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453478535i/17833133._SY540_.png" alt="f5fcaa09a848bf8c79aaf4590520ca13" width="496" height="621" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The deepest smile on my face, the lightest feeling I've had for the longest while, a warmness surrounding my heart... these were the things I've felt while AND after reading this book. I went from <em>"Hmmm, this is interesting!"</em> to <em>"OMFG THIS IS THE CUTEST!!! MY HEART!!! ASDFGHJKL;"</em> in like a fraction of a second once the book reeled me in its grasp. And trust me, it didn't even try.<strong> It was just absolutely, 100% effortless. </strong><br><br><strong>In other words: this book is a bloody gem.</strong><br><br>I've loved so many books in the past years, a fair amount of them contemporaries. And many of the contemporaries I've super enjoyed - like <em>Faking Normal</em>, <em>Emily and Oliver, What We Saw - </em>the best I could give them were4 stars. The 5 stars that I've awarded is reserved for books like <em>Anatomy of a Misfit </em><em>- </em>books with such amazing narration that feels not only real but also so very authentic to the point that the teenage me of yesterday comes out of her hidden depths just to cry out, "This character is so me. Her feelings, her fears, her insecurities are so me. SHE <strong>IS</strong> ME!"<br><br><em>Tell Me Three Things</em> is that, in a nutshell. I love this book so much like you all wouldn't believe. I honestly was a little hesitant at first, but then, as I read 5 pages, the narration made me chuckle. Then I started enjoying it, nodding my head and giggling every few minutes and going, "Holy heck, this narration is so deep and genuine and teenagery and not pretentious at all!" <strong>Then I started feeling it, loving it, adoring it, along with my teenage self that, once again, has wished that she read this kind of book when she was still trying fit herself in a world she could hardly begin to understand. </strong>And to top it all off? It was all of these things and it was such a light-hearted and cute story, to boot. I resonated with the characters AND felt incredibly giddy about everything, too.<br><br>The romance, the character and relationship development, the hows and whys of online connections... man. How do I even begin?<br><br>I already mentioned about how the narration was top-notch (it really is. I wish I could highlight pretty much every word here because they're just so awesome), <strong>but I'd also like to reiterate and emphasize how the narration as well made the issues being tackled here so very real and authentic. </strong>There's just something so simple and yet so melodic about Jessie's voice that makes her feel like she could be your friend or your neighbor or simply yourself (I'm not even a funny person when I was a teenager [and Jessie is, effortlessly, even if her humor is more self-deprecating than anything else], and yet!!!!), talking about out her fears and concerns as you would have talked about them, too. <strong>This is the number one reason (plus her bring adorably funny) that makes this book so close to my heart, and it's so hard to find a narration like that - something that doesn't pretend to be "lyrical" and "real" but is just effortlessly is.</strong><br><br>Imagine yourself as the new kid on the block, surrounded by people you don't know, far away from your best friend. You have a new mom who you're not yet ready to accept just yet, a new brother who wants to forget your existence, and your dad is way too busy "trying to move on" with his life without your real mom to understand the things you're going through. And then someone anonymously sends you a message, wanting to be the person to guide you through this new life you've stumbled yourself into, and as you get to know each other, you form a bond with someone you've never seen, never heard, never held. And you wonder, is this right?<br><br>Imagine that now with the most amazing narration... <strong>
  <em>ever</em>
</strong>.<br><br>The aspect with the anonymous friend over the internet was seriously so well-done. I know how there are books out there with text messaging and social media involved in their stories, but none felt so "connecting" and "right" as the one here. I love how it showed how on the internet, we can be anyone we want to be, in a sort of way. <strong>In real life, you limit yourself to the kind of person you think you can survive as (as the elusive kid who ignores everyone, for example) but once online, you're so happy-go-lucky and vibrant, because the shadow of anonymity gives us the sort of freedom to show the real us to the people we want to reveal ourselves to. </strong>And I love how this was tastefully done, and how it was a big part of the book's suspense, and how it made the story so cuter and exciting on top of being so funny, authentic, and real.<br><br>PLUS, DID I MENTION HOW IT'S SO DARN CUTE?! I WAS SMILING SO WIDELY BY THE END OF THE STORY, DAMNIT.<br><br>This book surprised me in the best way possible. I don't regret accepting the review request even one bit because it was so very worth it. Julie Buxbaum is now an insta-buy for me, and I have no doubt she will be an insta-buy for you guys as well once you get a dose of this beautiful, funny, cute, light-hearted story.<br><br><b>FOLLOW ME ALL OVER THE INTERWEBZ!</b><br><a href="Http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net" rel="nofollow noopener">The Social Potato</a> | <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> | <a href="http://notsoliterary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Not So Literary</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/user/dsocialpotatoreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://twitter.com/kawaiileena" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/fayemat" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/TheSocialPotatoReviews?ref=hl" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="http://ask.fm/fayelapatata" rel="nofollow noopener">Ask.fm</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2566349995555624116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="may ❀" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49148508-may"><img alt="may ❀" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562443036p2/49148508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1651270847?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="may ❀" class="user" itemprop="url" name="may ❀" href="/user/show/49148508-may">may ❀</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1651270847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6760424320617402366">I have just one question. <br/><br/>Where can I find myself a SN???????<br/><br/>I’m pretty big on the contemporary genre. It’s my <i>feel good </i> genre, it’s my <i>get-me-out-of-a-reading-slump </i> genre, it’s my <i>help-me-in-drowning-in-feels </i> genre. But lately . . . it’s been letting me down. <br/><br/>Maybe I’m becoming one of those cynical readers who criticizes everything (*screams*) but finding a realistic, relatable contemporary that has a good message and is enjoyable to read just seems so difficult lately. <br/><br/>. . . .until now . . </span>
  <span id="freeText6760424320617402366" style="display:none">I have just one question. <br><br>Where can I find myself a SN???????<br><br>I’m pretty big on the contemporary genre. It’s my <i>feel good </i> genre, it’s my <i>get-me-out-of-a-reading-slump </i> genre, it’s my <i>help-me-in-drowning-in-feels </i> genre. But lately . . . it’s been letting me down. <br><br>Maybe I’m becoming one of those cynical readers who criticizes everything (*screams*) but finding a realistic, relatable contemporary that has a good message and is enjoyable to read just seems so difficult lately. <br><br>. . . .until now . . . .<br><br>My happiness has been RESTORED. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450906897ra/17483210.gif" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay, this book, this book, this book. I don’t need to tell you that you NEED to pick it up right now. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490528127i/22321061._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It’s so bloody cute. <i> Tell Me Three Things </i> is about Jessie Holmes and her messed up junior year. With the death of her mom still taking a toll on her, her dad marries some rich, fancy lady and moves them from Chicago to LA. Everything is SUPER intimidating and Jessie is seriously homesick. <br>. . .then SN emails her. <br><br>SN (Somebody Nobody) is the sweetest, cutest human being you’ve ever met. This is a fact. <br><br>I CAN’T DEAL WITH MY FEELS TOWARDS THIS BOOK.<br><br><blockquote> Okay, okay quickly, let’s list all things great about this:<br>-	relatable on SO many levels<br>-	hilariously awkward and adorable <br>-	all the characters are dealing with ish<br>-	character G R O W T H<br>-	SN<br>-	the mystery behind SN<br>-	text banter<br>-	the ‘three’ things<br>-	friendships<br>-	family<br>-	amazing<br>-	cute<br>-	super cute<br>-	melts my heart<br>
</blockquote><br><br>Now, as much as I love this book with all my heart and I was willing to sacrifice my sleep for it, I have to mention the problems.<br><br>In the beginning, there was A LOTof <b> girl hate </b> and of course the whole love-triangle thing BUT SURPRISINGLY THE LOVE TRIANGLE DIDN’T BOTHER ME wow im a changed person<br><br>The fact of the matter is. . .<br>. . . if you love yourself, read this book.<br><br><i> “A rose is a rose is a rose. Jessie is Jessie is Jessie.” </i><br><br>4.5 stars and my sappy heart!!!<br><br><br>Another <i> <b> buddy read </b> with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29249069-pragya" rel="nofollow noopener">Pragya</a> </i> bc i MESSED UP WITH THE SCHEDULE damn me</span>

<div id="review_1601175632" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1601175632" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1601175632?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1826264879" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17762434587039788935"><b> 3.75 stars! </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “Just because you're strong doesn't mean you shouldn't ask for help sometimes. Remember that.” </i> </b><br/><br/>This book is the straight version of Simon Vs. the Homo-sapiens Agenda, and while they are very similar, it actually didn't bother me that much. I enjoyed each book for different reasons.<br/><br/>Tell Me Three Things is about a girl named Jessie whose mother died a couple years ago and now her father has found new love. This means selling her childhood home and moving to LA to live with her new </span>
  <span id="freeText17762434587039788935" style="display:none"><b> 3.75 stars! </b><br><br><b> <i> “Just because you're strong doesn't mean you shouldn't ask for help sometimes. Remember that.” </i> </b><br><br>This book is the straight version of Simon Vs. the Homo-sapiens Agenda, and while they are very similar, it actually didn't bother me that much. I enjoyed each book for different reasons.<br><br>Tell Me Three Things is about a girl named Jessie whose mother died a couple years ago and now her father has found new love. This means selling her childhood home and moving to LA to live with her new stepmother and stepbrother and leaving everything she knows behind. A few days into her new school and Jessie gets an anonymous message, reaching out to her to help her, but never divulging their identity.<br><br>Jessie begins to rely more and more on SN, and as time goes by adjusting to her new school gets easier. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458616698i/18508485.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> <i> “Perfect days are for people with small, realizable dreams. Or maybe for all of us, they just happen in retrospect; they're only now perfect because they contain something irrevocably and irretrievably lost.” </i> </b><br><br>I think this is a book a lot of teens (and adults) can relate to because it's all about coping in new environments and feeling like you're alone. Jessie is a very relatable character, trying to navigate a new school and a whole new family when she feels no one is on her side.<br><br>I will say I guessed who SN was fairly easily, I won't tell you how because spoilers. But even pretty much knowing who it was I enjoyed the book. I wish more had been developed in this book, like Jessie's relationship with her dad and her new family, I felt a lot of that was brushed over or quickly wrapped up. It was a huge part of her life and it seemed second to her issues in high school (which were just as bad, but still).<br><br>A quick read if you want to read something cute with a good ending.<br><br><b> <i> “Other people can't make you feel stupid. Only you can.” </i> </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455783307i/18148833._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="17762434587039788935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

That’s realistic enough, I guess. <br/><br/>But then literally everyone a</span>
  <span id="freeText2299205442695335642" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars</b><br /><br />What I expected:<br /><br /><blockquote>a) a super cute romance<br />b) a very fun read<br />c) something to smile about<br />✘ d) all of the above</blockquote><br />What I got:<br /><br /><blockquote>a) a super cute romance<br />b) a very fun read<br />c) something to smile about<br />✘ d) none of the above</blockquote><br />I love when books disappoint me!!!!!!!<br /><br /><blockquote>🌷 <b><u>ANNOYING STEREOTYPES</u></b></blockquote><br />So you have the MC named Jessie. She recently moved from Chicago (I think) to some fancy place in California. Her stepmom is rich, and she has a big fancy house. That’s realistic enough, I guess. <br /><br />But then literally everyone at her new school seems to be blond??? Everyone wears designer clothing??? Like can you calm down and include some diversity. It’s CALIFORNIA. There’s not only going to be white people in a state that big. Literally the only bit of diversity I remember was Jessie’s gay brother and that was it.<br /><br />Oh and not to mention, every blonde !! popular !! girl is going to be super mean and have a clique and flirt with all the boys!!!!!<br /><br /><blockquote>🌹 <b><u>GIRL HATE</u>????</b></blockquote><br />There was SO. MUCH. GIRL. HATE. <br /><br />I swear, there were five girl-hating statements in the span of two pages. Like no, shut up, we’ve established that all girls are amazing and should be loved and to be like “that girl” shouldn’t &amp; doesn’t mean anything because WE’RE ALL BEAUTIFUL. Can we PLEASE stop with this toxic mindset??<br /><br />All the girl hate was only in the beginning of the book, but I still wanted to gouge my eyes out and throw the book across the room. I couldn’t find myself liking Jessie after that oops.<br /><br /><blockquote>🌷 <b><u>MIXED FEELINGS ABOUT THE ROMANCE</u></b></blockquote><br />SN was SO. PREDICTABLE. The reviews I’ve read also said it was predictable. So what is the POINT of reading the book if you’ve already guessed everything??? Like, as soon as we met a certain character, I immediately thought, <i>That’s him. That’s SN. I can stop reading the book now.</i><br /><br />BUT. I do have to admit that it was <i>kinda</i> cute??? It was cute and fluffy. And it was super cringy, but you couldn’t keep yourself from liking it. All the emails were funny and a little adorable.<br /><br />SN made the romance cute. Jessie, on the other hand… uhhh probably one of the stupidest YA characters I’ve read, and that’s a lot???<br /><br />How does she think that SN is all these other dudes??? I, an outsider who does not care one bit about this story, figured it out from like, page 10. And then there was one scene where at the end where she literally must’ve fainted or something because she missed the VERY OBVIOUS clue about who SN is!!!! You dumb piece of crap!!!!<br /><br /><blockquote>🌹 <b><u>RELATABILITY</u></b></blockquote><br />However, even though Jessie is extremely stupid, I was able to really connect to Jessie’s mother’s cancer situation, because my own mom has cancer. (If anyone’s wondering, she’s in remission and is completely healthy lmao.) So I found that part really relatable!!<br /><br />Jessie was ALSO cool in terms of being a book nerd, and working at a bookstore and saying that it’s her dream job… because same.<br /><br /><br />So, it’s yet another disappointing read for me. But if you can ignore the girl hate, stereotypes, and stupidity of the main character, this one is for you!!! I have to admit that it is a somewhat cute romance (tho Jessie ruined it) and is somewhat enjoyable. Somewhat.<br /><br />Lowered from 3 stars to 2.5 stars because I’m indecisive!!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2299205442695335642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2193239825?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780399552939" href="/book/show/28925563-tell-me-three-things">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=easy-read">easy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=unexpectedly-good">unexpectedly-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=auto-buy-authors">auto-buy-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2193239825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5683173222438737771"><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25893582.Tell_Me_Three_Things' title='Tell Me Three Things by Julie Buxbaum' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tell Me Three Things</a> is one of the most relatable YA contemporaries I’ve read this year. The story line is simple, the plot not so eventful and yet it’s everything. It’s so easy to connect with <b>Jessie</b>, a teenage girl who just like any other girl is simply trying to figure out who she is. It isn’t easy being a teenager as it is but having to lose her mom at such a tender age and having to adjust to a new life that is very different from what she’s known- new home, new stepmom and step brother, I </span>
  <span id="freeText5683173222438737771" style="display:none"><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25893582.Tell_Me_Three_Things" title="Tell Me Three Things by Julie Buxbaum" rel="nofollow noopener">Tell Me Three Things</a> is one of the most relatable YA contemporaries I’ve read this year. The story line is simple, the plot not so eventful and yet it’s everything. It’s so easy to connect with <b>Jessie</b>, a teenage girl who just like any other girl is simply trying to figure out who she is. It isn’t easy being a teenager as it is but having to lose her mom at such a tender age and having to adjust to a new life that is very different from what she’s known- new home, new stepmom and step brother, I doubt I’d handle things any better than she did in the story. <br /><br />I like the story a lot because even though one of the main themes of the story is about grief, it doesn’t overpower the plot. In fact, it wasn’t a sad read at all. If anything, grief was just a platform for the main characters to influence each other to move forward. The main narrative devices used are e-mailing/IMing/ texting and well, it’s not difficult to enjoy it especially because of this mystery guy guiding Jessie navigate her new intimidating prep school via email/text. Of course, the mystery was quite predictable but still, I enjoyed trying to figure out who it is. The friendship bit is quite commendable too. <br /><br />Although at first I thought Jessie was an annoying, whiny teenager, it wasn’t long before my heart warmed up to her. I was a lot like her when I was younger- too insecure, too unsure of herself, too much whiteheads. The whiteheads are still there actually. Lol. But sometimes even when we think too little of ourselves, there are people who see, appreciate and acknowledge good things about us. Sometimes it takes an outside POV to make us appreciate what we have both inside and out. <br /><br />All thanks to Ms. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2082388937?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Kelly’s</a> super review for convincing me to read the book. &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="5683173222438737771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="mollusskka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37421969-mollusskka"><img alt="mollusskka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593311853p2/37421969.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37421969-mollusskka?shelf=gaya-cerita-bagus">gaya-cerita-bagus</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1719392649" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17643268011039374235"><b>
  <i>Tell me three things I don’t know about you.</i>
</b><br/><br/>Jessie is having the worst time of her life. At least, that's what she thinks. She's (still) been dealing with her mom's death since the last two years and her father remarried with a rich woman who lives in L.A. So, without even having a chance to speak her mind, she moves to this new, strange and luxurious house. Yes, you read it right. LUXURIOUS and Jessie don't feel good about it. (Well, clearly she's not me. I get it) And she's having a hard t</span>
  <span id="freeText17643268011039374235" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Tell me three things I don’t know about you.</i>
</b><br /><br />Jessie is having the worst time of her life. At least, that's what she thinks. She's (still) been dealing with her mom's death since the last two years and her father remarried with a rich woman who lives in L.A. So, without even having a chance to speak her mind, she moves to this new, strange and luxurious house. Yes, you read it right. LUXURIOUS and Jessie don't feel good about it. (Well, clearly she's not me. I get it) And she's having a hard time adapting with her new school and she's bullied. Until one day someone with an alias Somebody Nobody/SN sends her an email. Since then they become online friends. And of course they finally meet in real life. <br /><br />And now let me <b>TELL YOU THREE THINGS</b> about this book:<br /><br />1. I hate how it started with numbers. I suck at numbers and the author already made me count the days. It confused me already. But after these numbers stuff, the writing style is good. I had a good time reading this novel. It's cute and all that. And there's something deep about it. As I wrote above, it's about losing someone you really love and how it leaves you with pain on the inside. And it stays there even when you're living your life like everything's okay. And that "Dear Reader" note did touch my heart. So it's real that it takes years to let go. But somehow I think the author didn't deliver it very well. It just went in the wrong way and not so gripping. That I thought Jessie's sometimes so hard to believe. Are you serious about your grief? You need one example? Okay. Here: I don't understand how Jessie could be so randy about boys, especially Ethan, (she wants to kiss his ear lobe) and thinking about dating a boy name Caleb just at the first time she saw him. And the way Jessie narrated the story... She's too cheerful to be a girl in sorrow. Thank God she loves reading and works in a bookstore that I didn't turn to dislike her. And instead of Jessie, I like Agnes and Dri more. <br /><br />2. I don't understand the fact that Liam, Ethan and Caleb are parts of the band yet they never seem to hangout together. They often walk on their own. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I know Liam has a thing with Ethan, and Caleb is not an official member of the band, but still. They never really picture together <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and it made the uncovering of mysterious SN in the end is lame. So lame. Because honestly this mysterious SN is my main interest in this novel that kept me going. And how did Theo, not play a bigger part in this story? He's her stepbrother and they kinda hated each other. There should've been a better explanation about their lives together. <br /><br />3. I don't understand Scarlet. (And she has Korean blood! I mean, really?! Enough with the K-pop thing, please!) She and Jessie texted in a good vibe but when Jessie came to visit her, suddenly it was like she didn't want Jessie there. What is wrong with these people? And when Scarlet said Jessie only whined about her life while they were texting, that wasn't true. Jessie did asked about her life too, like how's she doing with Adam and all that. Yes, I'm on Jessie's side here. And what happened to Jessie at her visit did make me sad (And I think this is the best part of the story) How could two besties be like that? And they only two months separated, not years. So, come on! Grow up! <br /><br />I'm done with my three things. Now how about the ending? <br /><br />I like the ending. Everything's solved. Not so special, but at least it has something to say to people dealing with loss and having a hard time adapting with a new life. And I hope you'll have a good time reading this novel if you decide to read it. See you ^^<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17643268011039374235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3203090046" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3203090046?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>
