        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3203090046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12163729383628129332">Somewhere between 3.5 and 4 stars.<br/><br/>If only we could say the things we most need and want to, to those who most need to hear it.<br/><br/>"...I will continue to power through it—all the stagnant, soul-crushing grief—but it will never be okay that my mom is not here. That she will not be at my high school graduation; that she will never give me <i>the</i> lecture, and I won't be able to play along and pretend to be embarrassed and say, <i>Come on, Mom</i>; that she will not be there when I open my college acceptance lette</span>
  <span id="freeText12163729383628129332" style="display:none">Somewhere between 3.5 and 4 stars.<br /><br />If only we could say the things we most need and want to, to those who most need to hear it.<br /><br />"...I will continue to power through it—all the stagnant, soul-crushing grief—but it will never be okay that my mom is not here. That she will not be at my high school graduation; that she will never give me <i>the</i> lecture, and I won't be able to play along and pretend to be embarrassed and say, <i>Come on, Mom</i>; that she will not be there when I open my college acceptance letters (or rejections); that she will never see who I grow up to be—that great mystery of who I am and who I am meant to be—finally asked and answered. I will march forth into the great unknown alone."<br /><br />In <b>
  <i>Tell Me Three Things</i>
</b>, Jessie’s life has been totally uprooted. Her mom died, her dad has gotten remarried to a woman he met online, and has moved them from Chicago into her fancy Los Angeles home with her sullen, disapproving son. And perhaps worse than that, she has to start her junior year at a private high school where everyone is rich and confident and looks like a model.<br /><br />On her first day of school already in the midst of embarrassing disaster after embarrassing disaster, insult after insult, she gets an email from someone calling themselves “Somebody Nobody,” or “SN.” They claim to be a fellow student and offer to help Jessie navigate the wilds of the high school, anonymously of course.<br /><br />Little by little, Jessie starts to depend on SN, like him even, but she’s desperate to know who he is. She's finding it difficult to build her own life in California without him. And as she deals with bullying and self-confidence crises and unwanted attention from a friend and issues with her dad and the new life he’s dropped her in, she wants SN in real life more than ever, even as she’s fighting her IRL attraction to a classmate.<br /><br />This is a sweet book with a lot of poignancy, and as with many YA novels, the characters are funny and far more erudite than typical teens. Julie Buxbaum knows how to tug at your emotions without getting maudlin. (Her latest book, <b>
  <i>Hope and Other Punchlines</i>
</b>, really blew me away.)<br /><br />I pretty much predicted how this would resolve itself early on, and while I wasn’t disappointed with that resolution, I thought it took a little too long for the payoff. But the book was still fun and a quick read.<br /><br />Check out my list of the best books I read in 2019 at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2020/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2019.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2020/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2019.html</a>. <br /><br />Check out my list of the best books of the decade at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2020/01/my-favorite-books-of-decade.html" target="”_blank”" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2020/01/my-favorite-books-of-decade.html</a>.<br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>.<br /><br />Follow me on Instagram at <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the.bookishworld.of.yrralh/" target="”_blank”" rel="nofollow noopener"> https://www.instagram.com/the.bookishworld.of.yrralh/.</a></span>

<div id="review_1409292195" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1409292195" />
    <a title="Jaime Arkin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5293701-jaime-arkin"><img alt="Jaime Arkin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303353688p2/5293701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1409292195?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaime Arkin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaime Arkin" href="/user/show/5293701-jaime-arkin">Jaime Arkin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=galley-arc">galley-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=stand-alone-books">stand-alone-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=random-house">random-house</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1409292195" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2789578294223694860">Tell Me Three Things:<br/>1.	I will definitely be reading more of Julie Buxbaums YA stories.<br/>2.	I kind of read this whole story in just one day.<br/>3.	I absolutely adore Jessie. <br/><br/>If you don’t have this book on your radar yet, please make sure you add it to your to read list immediately. <br/><br/>I was pleasantly surprised by Buxbaum’s debut YA novel and I think that a lot of people are going to fall in love with her writing and this story once it’s out. <br/><br/>Jessie has had her life flipped upside down over the last few </span>
  <span id="freeText2789578294223694860" style="display:none">Tell Me Three Things:<br />1.	I will definitely be reading more of Julie Buxbaums YA stories.<br />2.	I kind of read this whole story in just one day.<br />3.	I absolutely adore Jessie. <br /><br />If you don’t have this book on your radar yet, please make sure you add it to your to read list immediately. <br /><br />I was pleasantly surprised by Buxbaum’s debut YA novel and I think that a lot of people are going to fall in love with her writing and this story once it’s out. <br /><br />Jessie has had her life flipped upside down over the last few years… the death of her mother two years ago was just the beginning. Now her father’s suddenly met someone new and married her of all things. But that’s not the only surprise. They’re selling the house she grew up in in Chicago and moving to L.A. for her junior year of high school and she gets no say in the whole mess.<br /><br />Leaving her best friend Scarlett behind, she’s forced to navigate the crazy that is Wood Valley High School, but someone is willing to offer her some guidance … anonymously. SN (Somebody/Nobody) is a mystery and while this person knows exactly who she is, Jessie is at a loss and trying to figure out who he/she just might be. <br /><br />So yes, part of this story is following along with Jessie and trying to figure out who this kind soul is. I have to admit that I pretty much had the person pegged pretty early on, that said, I was still pleasantly surprised with how much I still enjoyed it. <br /> <br />I really loved Jessie. Her grief for her mother is heartbreaking and having to give up everything familiar without any thought to how it will affect her had me wanting to pull her father aside and say “really?” I loved that eventually she and her father had it out and when she said she was allowed to be angry… I seriously wanted to hug her and say yes… yes you are! <br /><br />Being that Jessie is now in an exclusive private high school so of course I was expecting the mean girls that she experiences. I wish we had a bit more reasoning behind the way Gem and her friends all treat her so horribly. (Is it because she’s not like them?) I will say that I loved the bond she had with Dri and Scarlett and ultimately Agnes though I was sort of confused about her role in the book, possibly to show that Dri wouldn’t be replacing Scarlett in any way (I believe she says at one point that Agnes is Dri’s Scarlett?)<br /><br />Can I also say that I wanted more Theo? I love the bond that formed between him and Jessie despite the way things may have started (temper tantrum anyone?). They were good for each other and it was lovely to see the way their relationship develop.<br /><br />Buxbaum is definitely going to be an author to watch in YA. She manages to tell a story filled with depth and sadness and yet it’s light and funny and sweet. The story never overwhelmed me with sadness even though there was sadness within it. A quick paced story with a bit of a mystery will have readers turning pages quickly and finding a story of love, friendship and acceptance that fans of Rainbow Rowell and Becky Albertalli will definitely enjoy! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2789578294223694860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=physical-book-wishlist-want-it-need">physical-book-wishlist-want-it-need</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2065529318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7925062992700475726"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Perfect days are for people with small, realizable dreams. Or maybe for all of us, they just happen in retrospect; they’re only now perfect because they contain something irrevocably and irretrievably lost.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/>I’m going to be frank with you all: I never had <u>any</u> intentions of reading this novel. Nope. None. And then…and then I got on this kick where <b>I’m obsessed with online romance types</b> (or even love letter/pen pal types *see Punk 57/Letters to the Lost*) where two people are completely </span>
  <span id="freeText7925062992700475726" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Perfect days are for people with small, realizable dreams. Or maybe for all of us, they just happen in retrospect; they’re only now perfect because they contain something irrevocably and irretrievably lost.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />I’m going to be frank with you all: I never had <u>any</u> intentions of reading this novel. Nope. None. And then…and then I got on this kick where <b>I’m obsessed with online romance types</b> (or even love letter/pen pal types *see Punk 57/Letters to the Lost*) where two people are completely anonymous and know each other in real life-<u>but they don’t realize it</u>. And it’s so funny because I didn’t even realize I was gravitating to this type of book until I had read a handful. <br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>Me: So… <br />Scarlett: If you must know… <br />Me: I MUST, I MUST. <br />Scarlett: My hymen is intact. <br />Me: Surely you could have told me in a less graphic fashion.</blockquote>
</b><br /><br />So there I was, posting a review on GR and my blog for one of these types of books, then one of our followers on the blog commented on my review and said they had read this and liked it (THANK YOU, BEAUTIFUL PERSON, THANK YOU). So, naturally, I immediately switched over to GR, marked TM3T ‘to read’ and bought it immediately. And I must tell you: <b>It was love at first page</b>.<br /><br />I don’t know. Maybe it’s my new, beautifully hectic life or maybe my mind needed a break-who knows? But finding and attaching to this trope came at the best time. And I can’t necessarily pick a favorite out of the pile of cyber/letter books I’ve read in 2017, but each one always gives me the absolute best feelings. Where Punk was hot, dirty, hate-to-love romance, <b>TM3T was sweet, exploratory, one-sided, slow-build romance</b>. It was fun, flirty and made me smile so many times I can’t even count. I won’t lie-even though I’m living the dream, at the moment, I still have dark or heavy times. I don’t have all good days….so this book was just-It was such a fun, beautiful, shining light of a story and I gobbled up every page of it.<br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>He just nods again, like I’ve said yes. Like he asked and I answered a question. Right. Maybe not so nice after all. “But—” But what? <i>I was looking forward to being your partner? I like your serial killer eyes?</i><blockquote></blockquote></blockquote>
</b><br /> <br />I think the most amazing parts of these online romances are the secrecy. There is just something <i>so fun</i> about one person knowing who you are and the other being totally oblivious, but still falling in love that makes me all <b>screechy and fangirlish</b>. Don’t ask me why. I don’t know. I SAID don’t ask why! I just love ‘em. I do. Shh. <br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote> Ethan: From Merriam-Webster: Tuber: “a short, thick, round stem that is a part of certain plants (such as the potato), that grows underground, and that can produce a new plant.”<br />Me: Huh. Kinda makes sense. The whole feeding a new life part of the poem. <br />Ethan: But why are they dried? <br />Me: No idea. <br />Ethan: I like the word “tuber.” Makes a good insult. <br />Me: ??? Example, please. <br />Ethan: Gem and Crystal? Total tubers.</blockquote>
</b><br /><br />Now, it seems so odd that all these books always have one person who knows what’s going on and they lead the person they are crushing about on. I get that-but I think that’s my favorite thing. Is that weird? Whatever. Eliza knew about Wallace. Declan knew about Juliet. Misha knew about Ryen. Bailey and Porter knew about…well. They were oblivious way too long-ask my Frenchy Bug about that (SHUT UP. IF YOU DISS ON THE ONLY BOOKS I HAVE LOVED THIS YEAR I WILL END YOU [squish you like a], BUG). And, in a lot of these, there is anger. Betrayal. Hurt. Why didn’t the [secret] significant other admit they knew who the other was? Why keep up with the charade? And this proves to be an interesting plot point for me.<br /><br />All the authors handle the anger/betrayal/hurt differently, and I just always seem to love how it’s handled. It adds a layer of diversity to each book that makes me all giddy and weird-but, in the end, always incredibly happy. Because A) Wouldn’t you be pissed if someone you were falling for kept their identity a secret from you? And B) A lot of times, it’s the guy who knows first and he doesn’t like the girl in real life he thought he knew so well online. I LOVE THIS. Animosity from a broody man boy anyone? No takers? I’m the only weirdo? Cool. More Misha [etc.] for moi.<br /><br />But, that’s where TM3T differs-<b>it’s clear from the beginning</b>. The guy states he doesn’t want to be known and that he knows who she is and he just wants to help. They build a friendship, they grow closer, and they begin to fall in love….all the while she’s guessing/wishing/hoping about who it could be. See? All these books are so different…but the same. They all make me feel good and I truly think, for me, <b>that’s what makes me feel so alive</b>.<br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>Me: Do you think college will actually be better? For real? <br />SN: hope so. but then again, I just read about a guy who lost a ball in a frat hazing incident.<br />Me: Seriously? What is wrong with people?</blockquote>
</b><br /><br />But deeper than that, I love that these characters feel ‘less than’ because, in the end, they learn they don’t have to hide who they are-they don’t have to hide or change themselves to impress anyone else. And isn’t that why most people do the online thing? Because they are ashamed of themselves and don’t want people to know who they really are? It’s not necessarily a good message up front, but it always circles back to make it clear <b>we should be proud of who we are</b>. Maybe that’s reaching-but I like to think that’s the overall message in these books.<br /><br />But, again, this story differs in that way. This story is more about grief and getting past it-bonding over it and eventually finding out someone understands you and is there for you. It’s about friendship and healing and, finally, seeing there is a light at the end of the tunnel. Again, I’m reaching.<br /><br />All in all this is a super cute, fluffy contemporary that had me biting my lip and praying that Somebody Nobody was indeed who I hoped he’d be-and I was very pleased, thank you very much. SN was the unlikeliest of people to reach out and lend a virtual lending hand to help navigate the jungle of a new school when someone needed it most, and what followed was a story that <b>had me hooked from the start</b> and became possibly one of my favorites of the year. I finished in record time (since that’s now becoming two weeks for every book I read!!!) and devoured every word. I laughed and swooned and my heart went into overdrive. What else can you ask for?<br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>SN: you know what I think about sometimes? <br />Me: What? <br />SN: you know that piece of hair that always falls into your eyes—the not-quite-a-bang piece? I want to be able to tuck it behind your ear. I want to be able to do that. I want to meet you when I feel comfortable enough with you to do that.</blockquote>
</b><br /> <br />And I am SO SICK of people saying ‘just another young adult contemporary borrowed from books before it’ and that books are ‘nothing new’ and how they’ve ‘seen this before’. SO? Don’t all ideas come from somewhere? I am so sick of hearing this. Maybe this makes me naïve-but <b>I LIKE reading similar books to those I’ve loved before</b>. People need to chill. I’m sorry. But they do. All books can be said to be similar-just get <u>OVER</u> it. Seriously. All the books I love have this label from other reviewers yet they like books <i>IIII</i> find cliché-so who is in the wrong here? I don’t know. But what I do know? EVERY book builds on ideas other great authors have established years ago…no idea can be wholly unique, yet book after book gets pegged for being cliché and similar to others before it. But certain books are claimed to be so new and innovative, etc….I ain’t buyin’ it. I find those stories almost MORE generic. So. Meh. <br /><br />Oops. Ended my review on a rant-not my intention. But, as it were, I felt the winds of defensiveness on the tip of my tongue for my love of YA Contemporary. So take that as you will. I’ll just start yet another wonderful, not-so-new type of YA Contemp book. Come at me-because, frankly, I’ll probably love it, too. Shocker.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7925062992700475726" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

So I had a strong feeling I was going to love this, and I did.<br/><br/>Even though there were a few *minor* things that I didn't love... like Jessie's attitude sometimes (she did grow throughout and since it'd be stupid of me to expect a perfect MC, once she started changing I wasn't bothered by her) and <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ the multiple guys who were suddenly interested in the girl who'd never been no</span></span>
  <span id="freeText16990089225437723349" style="display:none">I need to start off by saying that I LOVE this trope. It's random, but I love the whole secret admirer plot. So I had a strong feeling I was going to love this, and I did.<br><br>Even though there were a few *minor* things that I didn't love... like Jessie's attitude sometimes (she did grow throughout and since it'd be stupid of me to expect a perfect MC, once she started changing I wasn't bothered by her) and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the multiple guys who were suddenly interested in the girl who'd never been noticed before  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, those were easy to overlook because of how much I loved the overall plot.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462950030ra/19063282.gif" width="350" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The storyline was fairly predictable, but I still felt invested and I found that I didn't mind that it was easy to figure out what was going to happen. I still really, <i>really</i> enjoyed this book. :) I loved watching all the characters change and grew and mend, and I kept reading for the character development as much as the satisfying conclusion. If you don't enjoy predictable storylines or this particular trope, you probably wouldn't enjoy this. But if you're like me, and you don't mind and/or you're as obsessed with secret admirers as I am, I'd definitely recommend it :)</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1888090596" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1888090596" />
    <a title="enqi ☁️✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41427900-enqi"><img alt="enqi ☁️✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604082105p2/41427900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1888090596?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="enqi ☁️✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="enqi ☁️✨" href="/user/show/41427900-enqi">enqi ☁️✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/26242642-tell-me-three-things">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41427900-enqi?shelf=2017-favs">2017-favs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41427900-enqi?shelf=certified-book-boyfriends">certified-book-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41427900-enqi?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41427900-enqi?shelf=amortentia">amortentia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41427900-enqi?shelf=on-my-kindle">on-my-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41427900-enqi?shelf=i-will-go-down-with-this-ship">i-will-go-down-with-this-ship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41427900-enqi?shelf=standalone-favorites">standalone-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41427900-enqi?shelf=standalones">standalones</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1888090596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6973227058928212408"><blockquote> <i> It is just him and me, Ethan is Ethan is Ethan and Jessie is Jessie is Jessie, and his lips touch mine. <br/><br/>But sometimes a kiss is not a kiss is not a kiss. Sometimes it's poetry. </i> </blockquote><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26242642.Tell_Me_Three_Things' title='Tell Me Three Things by Julie Buxbaum' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tell Me Three Things</a> is about a teenage girl, Jessie Holmes, who is still dealing with the aftermath of her mother's death and longs to find someone who can truly understand how she feels. Her dad remarries a rich woman, and she is uprooted to LA, leaving behind all her friends and her old life in Chicago. Jessie just </span>
  <span id="freeText6973227058928212408" style="display:none"><blockquote> <i> It is just him and me, Ethan is Ethan is Ethan and Jessie is Jessie is Jessie, and his lips touch mine. <br /><br />But sometimes a kiss is not a kiss is not a kiss. Sometimes it's poetry. </i> </blockquote><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26242642.Tell_Me_Three_Things" title="Tell Me Three Things by Julie Buxbaum" rel="nofollow noopener">Tell Me Three Things</a> is about a teenage girl, Jessie Holmes, who is still dealing with the aftermath of her mother's death and longs to find someone who can truly understand how she feels. Her dad remarries a rich woman, and she is uprooted to LA, leaving behind all her friends and her old life in Chicago. Jessie just doesn't fit in this fancy private Wood Valley High School, and she feels like everything about her is wrong. But then she gets an anonymous email from someone calling themselves Somebody/Nobody (SN), offering to help her navigate the wilds of WVHS. Is it an elaborate hoax? Or can Jessie rely on SN for some much-needed help? In a leap of faith, Jessie begins to rely on SN, and the two find that they have much in common. SN quickly becomes Jessie's friend and closest ally, and she can't help wanting to meet him. But will Jessie be disappointed when she finds out who he really is? Perhaps some mysteries are better left unsolved. <br /><br /><b> I will tell you three things about this wonderful book: </b><br /><br /><i> 1. It is hilarious and relatable and adorable and romantic and I couldn't stop smiling when I read it. </i> This story was impossibly cute, and from the very first page I was already grinning from ear to ear. I loved the banter between SN and Jessie. <br /><br /><blockquote> <i> "I have been watching you at school. not in a creepy way. though I wonder if even using the word "creepy" by definition makes me creepy? anyhow, it's just... you intrigue me." </i> </blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote> <i> SN: you know what I think about sometimes?<br /><br />Me: What?<br /><br />SN: you know that piece of hair that always falls into your eyes—the not-quite-a-bang piece? I want to be able to tuck it behind your ear. I want to be able to do that. I want to meet you when I feel comfortable enough with you to do that.<br /><br />Me: You are so weird.<br /><br />SN: you are not the first person to say that.<br /><br />Me: Am I the first to say that I really like that about you? </i> </blockquote> <br /><br />Jessie was so real. And this story was so heartbreaking and inspiring because of her. Jessie showed remarkable strength of character. Nothing in her new life was easy, yet still she took everything in her stride and never threw in the towel. I also love how down-to-earth and mature Jessie was, unlike the other snobs in her high school. She wasn't a hypocrite, or a drama queen, or anything like that. What Jessie did have was a sense of humor, and it was nice to be in her head. As the book continues, Jessie definitely grows as a person, and I adored her character arc and how she became comfortable in her own skin. <br /><br />Part of the reason why this book really spoke to me is Julie Buxbaum's heartfelt dedication at the end of the book. It sheds a whole new light on the story, knowing that the author experienced similar circumstances. It makes the tale more sincere. Although this book focuses on the aftermath of a great tragedy (Jessie's mom dying), it wasn't too gritty or depressing, which would have made it hard to get through. Instead, Julie Buxbaum incorporates this element of the plot seamlessly into the story without shoving it down the reader's throat, and this makes it easier for the reader to connect with and relate to Jessie even if they may not have experienced the loss of such a close family member. As a result, whenever Jessie's mind reverted to her mother, or the changes in her life since her mother's death, I only felt sympathy and empathy, not annoyance, because I could understand her emotions and thoughts.<br /><br />I loved several of the side characters in this book. Theo, Jessie's stylish hipster stepbrother, was an asshole in my very first impressions, but as the story progressed he became more likeable and less aloof, and was even decent to Jessie. He was one of my favorite characters. Dri, one of Jessie's newfound best friends, was everything I could ever want in a friend. And Agnes I thought was strange at first, but gradually grew to like her.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26242642.Tell_Me_Three_Things" title="Tell Me Three Things by Julie Buxbaum" rel="nofollow noopener">Tell Me Three Things</a> is different from other contemporary romances in that there was a slight element of mystery to it. Granted, I guessed who SN was about three chapters in and I'm shocked that it took Jessie 300 pages, but nevertheless, it still kept me flipping the pages as my curiosity intensified throughout the book. In the end, I was equal parts joyful and triumphant when I found out who he was.<br /><br /><i> 2. Dreamy male characters. </i> In this story we are introduced to three attractive boys, and Jessie wonders if any of them is SN at some point. I adored every moment of the romance in this book - it was unbelievably cute and I could almost see the sweetness dripping from the pages. SN was really someone who <i> knew </i> Jessie, a bedrock she could fall back on in times when she needed solace. I just love how Jessie was able to connect to him so powerfully, even though their interactions were purely from behind a screen. His replies were filled with humor and he seemed to know exactly what to say to cheer Jessie up. There was definitely a distinct connection between the two of them, and I was so excited every time their passages came up in the book.<br /><br />And the ending. The ending literally destroyed me in the best way. SN's reveal scene is so delightful and heartwarming that I was internally squealing over how lovely it was. I was overjoyed when I found out his identity - partly because I'd guessed it long ago but was unsure, and partly because I was so happy it was him, since I'd been having a crush on him right along with Jessie throughout the story. <br /><br /><i> 3. Why isn't there an epilogue?! I literally need one to happen. Now. </i><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26242642.Tell_Me_Three_Things" title="Tell Me Three Things by Julie Buxbaum" rel="nofollow noopener">Tell Me Three Things</a> is a book I loved so much and will keep in my heart. The story is deliciously sweet (like a waffle), heartwarming and romantic with a strong, inspiring heroine. Surprisingly, this book had almost no physical intimacy, with the only kiss happening on the last page (and even that scene was so adorable I had to blush). But I really enjoyed it nevertheless - I devoured this book in a day because I just couldn't put it down. Contemporary romances are mostly a hit or miss for me, but this one is definitely a hit.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6973227058928212408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=average">average</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=cute-and-or-easy-reads">cute-and-or-easy-reads</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1646823573" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16535206252658463422"><b> 3.5 / 5 ~</b><br/><br/> A perfect Valentine’s Day read; that’s what <i>Tell Me Three Things</i> is. It’s filled with relatable characters, a realistic main character, and funny banter. And although much doesn’t happen (in terms of action, drama, and all that jazz) and I found everything predictable, others might enjoy this book more than I did — especially if they don’t figure out who Somebody Nobody is around chapter two.<br/><br/>I loved reading through Jessie’s eyes (is that how you say it?). She’s honest, not perfect, ha</span>
  <span id="freeText16535206252658463422" style="display:none"><b> 3.5 / 5 ~</b><br /><br /> A perfect Valentine’s Day read; that’s what <i>Tell Me Three Things</i> is. It’s filled with relatable characters, a realistic main character, and funny banter. And although much doesn’t happen (in terms of action, drama, and all that jazz) and I found everything predictable, others might enjoy this book more than I did — especially if they don’t figure out who Somebody Nobody is around chapter two.<br /><br />I loved reading through Jessie’s eyes (is that how you say it?). She’s honest, not perfect, has insecurities, anger, and is hilarious. This books grabbed my attention because of her bluntness and <i>realness</i> from page one. Honestly, it was that fast.<br /><br />Somebody Nobody, the guy who sends Jessie an anonymous email telling her she’ll make it in the new prep school she’s going to, hit up an online friendship/relationship. The whole intrigue of the book is trying to figure out who this guy is — only I immediately knew who they were. I just knew. And I was right when it was revealed. But I won’t spoil that, because I think it would be fun for people to wonder who he is. <br /><br />All in all, there isn’t much of anything that happens that is inherently original or fascinating — it’s just a fun read. So if you’re looking for something romantic and relatable, I would definitely recommend this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16535206252658463422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1602015780" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1602015780" />
    <a title="Sharon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23218431-sharon"><img alt="Sharon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563502369p2/23218431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1602015780?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon" href="/user/show/23218431-sharon">Sharon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=eyeroll-moments">eyeroll-moments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=ugh">ugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=beautiful-covers">beautiful-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=been-there-done-that">been-there-done-that</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=love-that-cover">love-that-cover</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1602015780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10107037120048998078">Two minutes into the book, and I already <b>laughed, smiled like an idiot, and snorted</b>. All I was thinking was, "Why is this book so adorable????" <br/>...And then it went <b>downhill</b> after 5 minutes.<br/><br/><u>Pros</u><br/>-I'm a sucker for <b>romance-before-first-sight</b> where somehow the girl and guy start sending each other secret messages (in this case, email/IM)<br/>-Some <b>very cute bantering</b> such as:<br/><blockquote>
  <i>"I have been watching you at school. not in a creepy way. though I wonder if even using the word “creepy” by definition makes me </i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText10107037120048998078" style="display:none">Two minutes into the book, and I already <b>laughed, smiled like an idiot, and snorted</b>. All I was thinking was, "Why is this book so adorable????" <br />...And then it went <b>downhill</b> after 5 minutes.<br /><br /><u>Pros</u><br />-I'm a sucker for <b>romance-before-first-sight</b> where somehow the girl and guy start sending each other secret messages (in this case, email/IM)<br />-Some <b>very cute bantering</b> such as:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>"I have been watching you at school. not in a creepy way. though I wonder if even using the word “creepy” by definition makes me creepy? anyhow, it’s just…you intrigue me."</i>
</blockquote> <br />^^^This is the <b>most cute-creepy thing</b> I have ever read. LOL.<br />-The <b>friendships</b> are nice. I like that Jessie had Scar as her original best friend from her old school. I also like that there is this moment where Jessie realizes that Scar has been listening Jessie struggling without Scar, but Jessie is too self-absorbed to realize that Scar is lonely too. In addition, Jessie's best friend at her new school is cool too. Overall, nice friend support system.<br />-Theo. Jessie's stepbrother is <i>such</i> an asshole in the beginning, but he actually turns out to be <b>incredibly honest, funny, and supportive</b>. He is one of my favorite aspects about this book.<br />-I like the way the <b>family</b> conflict is resolved. Jessie and her dad learn to start talking and communicating again. They were struggling after Jessie's mom died, but it was good to see them finally find a place where they can communicate and be a family again. Also, the stepmother isn't as bad as she originally appeared, and I like that she and Jessie are willing to try to be better by the end of the book<br />-<b>Ending: Pretty damn cute.</b> It is just well-done and immensely adorable.<br /><br /><u>Cons</u><br />-The antagonist is the <b>cliché "mean, popular, pretty" girl who bullies the protagonist for things that don't matter</b>. I'm just not a fan of the trope where girls get petty and hate on other girls, especially out of jealousy FOR A GUY. Perhaps this is "realistic," and yes, many movies, books, plays, etc. love the theme of female jealousy and pettiness for a guy, but it's still not enjoyable. <br />-I don't like the comments Jessie make about other girls she sees at her school. <b>Some skinny-shaming, slut-shaming, girl-hating-on-girls, etc.</b> There are also some stereotyping. <br />-<b>Cliché and predictable plot</b>. Every conflict and resolution that happened in this book is not anything really new. I was rather bored for most of it, except for the very beginning and end. <br />-A lot of <b>silly, cliché attention on popularity/not-being-cool and mean girls being mean</b> just for funsies or because of a guy. Some people may argue that this is realistic - and I can somewhat see that. Yes, most (if not all) high schools have some form of popularity contest and of course, people being bullied in high school for no fuckin' good reason is a real thing (sadly). It's just not fun reading a book that focuses on this stuff for me personally. High school drama such as "being cool" and "mean girls" are just so... insignificant, in my opinion. It's realistic, and it makes sense for a 16-year-old to not be secure enough to not care about these things, but still, for my preference - not fun to read. (I like YA contemporary but not when it has too much emphasis on stuff like this)<br />-<b>Misunderstanding trope</b>. I don't even know how Jessie misunderstood that a certain guy was her secret emailer. She somewhat just assumed, and she didn't even bother clearing up, like "Hey. That was you in the shop today, right?" *facepalm*<br /><br />Overall, I'm giving <i>Tell Me Three Things</i> <b>2 stars</b>. I really do like the very beginning - it's funny and unbelievably cute. I was SO SURE I was going to adore this book with how much I smiled and laughed right off the bat. The ending is also on point. Unfortunately, I did not enjoy the book much throughout. I was bored and I didn't like a lot of the plotting and the "mean, pretty popular girl picks on the protagonist" trope. It's a mixed bag, but I'm sure some people would still enjoy it for some of the cute bantering.<br /><br /><u>Things that you might want to know <b>(WARNING: Spoilers below)</b></u><br />Is there a happy/satisfying ending? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Quite satisfying. Incredibly cute. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Love triangle? Cheating? Angst level? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Love...square-ish? Pentagon? Hexagon? I don't know. The girl has 3 potential love interests. One of those potentials already has a girlfriend. Another girl also has a crush on the potential who has a girlfriend. No cheating, I think. Medium angst. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Tears-worthy? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Some sad mentions of deaths (of family), but not too sad. No tears. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Humor? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Some cute bantering. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Favorite scene? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The very beginning. The very end. Super cute. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />What age level would be appropriate? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[At least teenager. Some mentions of sex, drug, and drinking. Not much details on anything. The protagonist's romance is very PG. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />-----<br />I haven't read a YA Contemporary/Romance in a while and I am quite excited. That cover is simply adorable &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="10107037120048998078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1498523236" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1498523236" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500935920p2/8472395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1498523236?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8472395-alyssa?shelf=2016-releases">2016-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1498523236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6368441040001587910">4.5 stars. 5 stars?<br/><br/>NO TRIANGLE. Or any kind of geometry. The synopsis is purposefully misleading - and for good reason!<br/><br/>Check out <strong>
  <a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2016/01/swoon-thursday-154-tell-me-three-things.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>a swoony excerpt</a>
</strong>!<br/><br/><br/><br/>***<a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2016/01/review-tell-me-three-things-by-julie.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br/><br/>Tell Me Three Things by Julie Buxbaum<br/>Publisher: Delacorte Press<br/>Publication Date: April 5, 2016<br/>Rating: 4 stars<br/>Source: ARC sent by the publisher<br/><br/>Summary (from Goodreads):<br/><br/>Everything about Jessie is wrong. At least, that’s what it feels like during her first week of junior year at her new ultra-intimidating</span>
  <span id="freeText6368441040001587910" style="display:none">4.5 stars. 5 stars?<br /><br />NO TRIANGLE. Or any kind of geometry. The synopsis is purposefully misleading - and for good reason!<br /><br />Check out <strong>
  <a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2016/01/swoon-thursday-154-tell-me-three-things.html" rel="nofollow noopener">a swoony excerpt</a>
</strong>!<br /><br /><br /><br />***<a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2016/01/review-tell-me-three-things-by-julie.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br /><br />Tell Me Three Things by Julie Buxbaum<br />Publisher: Delacorte Press<br />Publication Date: April 5, 2016<br />Rating: 4 stars<br />Source: ARC sent by the publisher<br /><br />Summary (from Goodreads):<br /><br />Everything about Jessie is wrong. At least, that’s what it feels like during her first week of junior year at her new ultra-intimidating prep school in Los Angeles. Just when she’s thinking about hightailing it back to Chicago, she gets an email from a person calling themselves Somebody/Nobody (SN for short), offering to help her navigate the wilds of Wood Valley High School. Is it an elaborate hoax? Or can she rely on SN for some much-needed help?<br /><br />It’s been barely two years since her mother’s death, and because her father eloped with a woman he met online, Jessie has been forced to move across the country to live with her stepmonster and her pretentious teenage son.<br /><br />In a leap of faith—or an act of complete desperation—Jessie begins to rely on SN, and SN quickly becomes her lifeline and closest ally. Jessie can’t help wanting to meet SN in person. But are some mysteries better left unsolved?<br /><br />What I Liked:<br /><br />I took a chance with this book; I'm not a YA contemporary person, and I knew that the romance in this book could go in several different directions. Obviously we all want her to end up with her secret emailing admirer (even without reading the book, you're rooting for him!), but we also know that the person emailing her might not be someone she likes away from the screen. So, I was worried about a love triangle or something of the sort. I am very happy to report that there was a very linear romance, and the story was beautiful and heart-wrenching and lovely!<br /><br />Jessie's mother died two years ago. Her father remarried, and now she and her dad are living in L.A. with his new (rich) wife Rachel, and Rachel's son Theo. Rachel is paying for Jessie to attend a very fancy and preppy private school, Wood Valley High School. Jessie's first week is a disaster, and most people noticed - specifically, an anonymous person referred to as Somebody/Nobody, who emails Jessie, encouraging her and telling her details about Wood Valley High. Jessie is wary at first, but finds herself chatting online with SN more and more. She wants to meet her peer, who knows who she is, and has been a friend throughout the rough transition. But what if the person behind the screen isn't someone she likes in real life?<br /><br />This book was absolutely stunning, inside and out. Can we just talk about the cover for a second? I thought it was interesting, when I first saw it, and that was one of the reasons why I accepted the book for review. But now that I've read the book, I can appreciate the cover even more. "Waffle" is Jessie's favorite word, and it has another significance in the book (several, actually). Love!<br /><br />Oh Jessie. Her pain and anger and frustration and numbness felt so real and tragic. I could see myself reacting exactly as she did, in terms of the big move, her father ignoring her feelings, her new stepmother, her new stepbrother, her new school. I love Jessie so much - she is someone to whom I can relate, someone real, someone likable. Even if you aren't entirely like her, you can relate to her on some level. Jessie is down-to-earth (especially compared to these snobs in Wood Valley High), intelligent, determined, hard-working, smart with money, humble... someone that I would be friends with, in real life. <br /><br />I LOVE how real all of Buxbaum's characters seemed to me! Wood Valley High is very different from my high school, yet the high school experience is (for the most part) is at least similarly and generally understood by most. This high school is filled with rich snobs, with perfect hair, model good looks, weird organic food... I've never been to L.A., but I can stretch my imagination and believe it. <br /><br />Anyway, secondary characters. Jessie's new friends Dri and Agnes are so sweet. Agnes is a little strange at first, but I liked her. Theo, Jessie's stepbrother, seems like a tool at first, but I warmed up to him quickly. He's actually a nice guy (though I still refuse to think of him as a "decent" guy). <br /><br />We have our potential SN guys: Caleb, a rando who doesn't really play a big role throughout the book, but is very convincingly like SN. Liam, a senior, who plays a larger role in the book, and has been nice to Jessie from the start. And Ethan, Jessie's English partner for a project, who is good-looking but also a bit cold. Distant? He plays a huge role in the book, especially as Jessie's partner for the English project. <br /><br />I'll just say it - there is no love triangle. Or square. Or pentagon, pyramid, rhombus, whatever. No geometry whatsoever, except for a straight line. The romance in this book is VERY linear. I love the romance, honestly. Jessie falls for this certain guy in real life, and she also develops a strong connection to SN. Whoever is behind the screen is someone that understands and cares about her, and by the climax of the book, Jessie is convinced that it's one of those three boys. I really like how the romance turned out. TRUST ME when I say that there is no love triangle. There is emotional and physical interaction only with one guy... the right guy. *wink*<br /><br />So that's the romance. And I mentioned the characters. I also loved the "tough-issue" story, how heartbreaking and inspiring the story is. Loving a parent, and then the other (to a stepmother), moving cross-country, starting over in a school filled with people that look down on you... nothing comes easy, for Jessie. I love her strength of character, and how she grows as the story continues. This book isn't so gritty and difficult to read that a non-contemporary person like me would stop reading. No, this book was beautiful and achingly sweet to read.<br /><br />I am so pleased with this book. The story is incredible, the heroine is so strong and inspiring, and the romance is really sweet, without having any physical intimacy (which is so great, in its own way). I kind of love how Jessie is able to connect with someone so powerfully, in this age of technology and behind-the screen interactions. I really adored this book!<br /><br />What I Did Not Like:<br /><br />I know I just said how I loved that this book had no physical intimacy in it (like the only kiss comes at the very end, in the "reveal" scene). BUT I also personally find this to be a negative because I looove physical interactions in a book that has such a great romance in it! However I can see how that wouldn't really fit, in this book. But still.<br /><br />Would I Recommend It:<br /><br />I so recommend this book! I'm not even a YA contemporary person, and I'm recommending it. Have you seen the amount of positive reviews on Goodreads? This book is so worth the buzz that has been floating around. Give it a chance! I tend to stay far away from YA contemporary - especially those dealing with "tough issues", but this book was really worth the read.<br /><br />Rating:<br /><br />4.5 stars -&gt; rounded down to 4 stars (I'm not really sure why I'm rounding down, but it doesn't quite feeling like a five-star read to me). Such a wonderful book, and a fast read, too! I'm glad I took a chance on this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6368441040001587910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1906465032" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1906465032" />
    <a title="Beatrice Masaluñga" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga"><img alt="Beatrice Masaluñga" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603719912p2/4590441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1906465032?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beatrice Masaluñga" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beatrice Masaluñga" href="/user/show/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga">Beatrice Masaluñga</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1906465032" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11169147712480165933"><i>Tell Me Three Things</i> is a delightful contemporary novel and here are three things I adore about this book:<br/><br/>1.) <b>The story is heartwarming and clever.</b> Two years ago, <b>Jessie Holmes</b> lost her mother due to Cancer and she's still grieving about it. When her father remarried a woman he met online, they move to California from Chicago. She lives with her stepmom and stepbrother, Theo. It's difficult for Jessie to adjust in a new environment especially she's attending her new school, Wood Valley High Scho</span>
  <span id="freeText11169147712480165933" style="display:none"><i>Tell Me Three Things</i> is a delightful contemporary novel and here are three things I adore about this book:<br /><br />1.) <b>The story is heartwarming and clever.</b> Two years ago, <b>Jessie Holmes</b> lost her mother due to Cancer and she's still grieving about it. When her father remarried a woman he met online, they move to California from Chicago. She lives with her stepmom and stepbrother, Theo. It's difficult for Jessie to adjust in a new environment especially she's attending her new school, Wood Valley High School. One day, she received an email from someone named <u>Somebody Nobody or SN</u>. As they exchange messages, she finds comfort talking to him. She haven't met him and wonders who is SN. <br /><br />2.) <b>Guessing who is SN.</b> Based on the conversations Jessie and SN have, there are three guys to choose from. This guessing game (quite cliche but I don't mind) is so entertaining! I placed my bet on this <i>one guy</i> and I got it wrong for not trusting my instinct. No regrets though because I enjoy it and the guy behind SN is adorable and witty. <br /><br />3.)<b>Chapter 34: The Last Chapter</b>. This is the highlight scene for me wherein SN's identity has been revealed. It's so cute and it made me smile. On the side note, I'm glad everything was resolved on the family aspect, friendship and grief. Jessie's character development is great and realistic as especially as she copes on loss. <br /><br />The reason I didn't give this 5 stars because of its pacing. It took me a while to get into the story until the 40% mark. Still, it's an enjoyable book and I recommend it to readers who enjoy YA contemporary novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11169147712480165933" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xyHCE+uBVTrJzKIT30HceMk2VjvniMME/7Q5e3BVoQGrIE+X1qf9y5wFnIlLnBUH4/l0Sy6hGvhyfoMbORajdA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0RIavqpQYEJVMiZiBmeICyllM1C7Pvt6gfrLiThX+c+9E5c6l3bIswD7GPiSukF0A6oRIHIXIoYMMHHpcRT7ug==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15549994843519819219">Julie Buxbaum is the New York Times best selling author of Tell Me Three Things, her young adult debut, What to Say Next, Hope and Other Punchlines, and Admission (pubs 5/5/20). She’s also the author of two critically acclaimed novels for adults: The Opposite of Love and After You. Her work has been translated into twenty-five languages. Julie’s writing has appeared in various publications, includ</span>
  <span id="freeText15549994843519819219" style="display:none">Julie Buxbaum is the New York Times best selling author of Tell Me Three Things, her young adult debut, What to Say Next, Hope and Other Punchlines, and Admission (pubs 5/5/20). She’s also the author of two critically acclaimed novels for adults: The Opposite of Love and After You. Her work has been translated into twenty-five languages. Julie’s writing has appeared in various publications, including The New York Times. She is a former lawyer and graduate of Harvard Law School and lives in Los Angeles with her husband, two children, and more books than is reasonable. Visit Julie online at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.juliebuxbaum.com">www.juliebuxbaum.com</a> and follow @juliebux on Twitter.</span>
